There are two setting for pressure, low and high.  I&#x27;ve never needed high as it does just fine on the low setting.  There&#x27;s no need for high pressures, just enough to remove the food particles.  The idea isn&#x27;t to drive the food particles into and under the gum tissues, just remove them with REGULAR Waterpik use.  My wife has a plug-in tank model and sets the pressure at about half which she says is plenty.     <li> I purchased a waterpikand it gave up, luckily before the guarantee ran out so I received another.This one lasted just a year and stopped working.I decided to try and repair it because other reviews said the battery stops charging, anyway I dismantled it which was pretty easy and found that the problem was water and dirt had got onto the contacts on the power button so cleaned them with a swab and put a little petroleum jelly on the contacts and now it works fine again.So it seems the battery isn&#x27;t to blame but water and dirt getting past the seals onto the contacts.  I think this is a good machine when it is working correctly but better sealing against water and debris would make them more reliable and last a lot longer.     <li> I was a happy user of WaterPik&#x27;s old travel oral irrigation system, the 350W. It had a detachable tank, and the tips were connected to the pump via flexible tubing, which was of course the system&#x27;s weak spot (the tubing would eventually crack). Aside from that, the system was exceptionally durable and lasted 9 years with only one change of tubing, which unfortunately is no longer available. Because of my good experience with the 350W, and because the WP-450 is rechargeable, I was inclined to prefer it over the Panasonic Oral Irrigator EW-DJ10-A.    I was wrong. The WP-450 is much bigger than the photos suggest, and rather unwieldy. It doesn&#x27;t appear to be particularly well-made. It&#x27;s also not inexpensive. Furthermore, there are inconveniences: for example, since the tank is detachable, one would expect to be able to fill the tank at the sink and then reattach it to the body, but the tank leaks water in this case because WaterPik didn&#x27;t see fit to put a simple valve on the tank&#x27;s water output. Another inconvenience which may only affect a small number of user is that although the WP-450 is described as a travel irrigator, its transformer only works with 120 VAC - the transformer that came with my 350W was dual-voltage.    I ordered the Panasonic Oral Irrigator EW-DJ10-A and found it superior to the WaterPik: a more elegant design, better construction, smaller and easier to handle. Also costs 1/3 less than the WaterPik. It only comes with one nozzle (and of only one type -- the WaterPik comes with 4 different ones), but that seems sufficient to me.</li>

    <li> I was ambivalent about buying this based on the reviews that I have read. I will say up front I do not have a Waterpik that sits on my counter top and plugs into the wall socket. It was OK but the battery pretty much had to be charged every week if used daily. It held just enough water to get the job done, it was hard to fill with water under the bathroom sink and I got about 3 years use from it until the unit stop charging due to corrosion where the charger plugs into the unit(This is because water spills on the connection).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  I then bought the Panasonic EW-1270AC. This was fine for travel but it had allot of problems like the water cap always falling off, water leaking out when you needed to store  it in the suitcase(always had to keep it in a zip loc bag to prevent the remaining water that was always there even after emptying in sink), the tip always falling on the floor as the way it was to be stored should have held the tip better. Coffee grinder loud!&lt;br /&gt;** Yes I guess it is loud as it is near you ear while using! I use mine for about 30 seconds until all food is removed and I still have half of the water left. And yes I am using the High pressure setting. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. The tip is so mobile (rotates all over the place), you can&#x27;t control it.&lt;br /&gt; ** Mine doesn&#x27;t. Of course I have only had it a month. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. It is poorly designed, too large, and difficult to hold (Can&#x27;t imagine if you have small hands).&lt;br /&gt;** I thought it was well ergonomically designed. I think it is most excellent! **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. Poor battery life, long charge time, no charge indicator. After two uses I needed to recharge! (yes I let it charge up initially for 16 hours!).&lt;br /&gt;** I have only charged my unit for 8 hours and have been using once a day for a month. I has not slacked off one bit in pumping the water out. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6. Expensive, Poor Value: Price is ~70% higher than the WP-360&lt;br /&gt;** Yes that is usually the case for older models. They usually do cost less than newer models as the cost of production is higher than years ago. It is actually 61.4 % higher in cost. The old unit uses Ni-Cad batteries as the new one uses more expensive L-Ion or NiMH batteries hence the higher cost and the L-Ion battery can hold a charge longer. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;7. Poor Reservoir Capacity -only 120 ml or 20% less than the already-tiny WP-360&#x27;s 150 ml&lt;br /&gt;** I do not know how you can say that. I fill my units up to max and the new Water Jet holds twice the amount of water then the WP-360. Also I had to use a paper cup the fill up the old WP-360 **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;8. Terrible portability, large/inefficient size, ungainly ergonomics&lt;br /&gt;** Well it is not touted as a travel water jet just a cordless one for home use. The Panasonic however is a true Travel/Portable unit as advertised. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;9. Weak water stream.&lt;br /&gt;** You&#x27;ve got to be kidding. It has two settings and is way better then the WP-360 and about the same pressure as the Panasonic model. Are you sure you have it charged up? **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;10. Very bad. Main problem is the tip won&#x27;t stay fixed, it keeps rotating, so it sprays water everywhere but your teeth.&lt;br /&gt;** I have not observed this problem. My tips stays right where it should. I will report back if this changes. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;11. The reservoir is so small that it empties before you are ready to stop using it. It should be at least 2 1/2 times the size.&lt;br /&gt;** I have to wonder what you are using this for. I use mine to remove the food particles from the gums and between teeth. When things stop coming out of the mouth am done. My dentist says I have the best gums of any patient he has in his practice and I only use this once a day before bed. **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  It appears that the problem with the old WP-360 was the fact that the charger contacts on the front would get water inside no matter how careful one was and the metal from the charger was different from the metal that took the charger. What I observed on the WP-360 was dissimilar metal corrosion. What I observed on this new water jet was the charger contact is now enclosed in plastic and has been moved to the back of the unit where their is less chance of water getting in to the charger contacts.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  Allot of people keep going on about the old WP-360 in this post about the batteries not holding a charge. I think most people probably keep the unit charger plug in while not in use. This will lead to what is called a memory problem with Ni-Cad batteries. Ni-Cad batteries should never be keep on a continuous charge as that will  lead to the memory problem mentioned. It is best to have Ni-Cads discharge completely and then recharge them. L-Ion / NiMH batteries do not suffer from this problem that I know of, but it is always better to only charge any battery after it loses its charge. Continuous charging on batteries will lead to shorten battery life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;  If I experience any problems with the Waterpic Water Jet WP-450 Ultra I will amend this review. I just can not understand all these bad negative reviews. If the unit was so bad why would it be the number one seller when I bought it? No I do not work for Waterpic but I have used their products for years and have not had that many problems which is why I guess they are still number one in Oral Irragtor sales. I hardily recommend the WP-450 Ultra if you are looking for a cordless (not Travel sized) waterjet. This is hands down better then the old but still selling WP-360.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Updated 20 June 2016:&lt;br /&gt;Been working great for the last 7 years!!!!!!!!!!e WP-360 and about the same pressure as the Panasonic model.     <li> It is what Waterpik claims it is.    Does it hold enough water?  First few uses, I wished it held more water, but after using it daily, I manage to waterpik every tooth and completely cover all gum&lt;&gt;tooth areas with one filling.     Will the battery hold up?  I charge it up, then unplug it and use it for days until it stops or shows signs of needing recharge, then recharge it and have not experienced battery issues yet.  All battery operated devices like this have tricky battery usage.  If Waterpik wants to know: please put a small LED-type battery strength indicator on the next model.  Without the battery indicator, I have had at least one morning where I was unable to finish using the waterpik and would have preferred knowing the night or day before that it should have been plugged in to charge overnight prior to that morning.     Does the rotation gizmo attachment work?  By design it seems that a user could easily move his/her thumb slightly to rotate the spout to either left or right and thereby more accurately cover all areas of the inside gums and teeth.  Well, it can work that way.  It is easier for me to simply leave the little spout in one place and hold the waterpik with two hands and very carefully trace the gum/tooth line for the top and bottom front and bottom back.  Then twist the spout 180 degrees when it is not in my mouth to prep it to cover the top inside areas.  It must be very uncomfortable and maybe ineffective for people to try to rotate that thing accurately with one thumb while it is in the mouth and they are moving it from side to side.      Is there enough water pressure generated?  I&#x27;m not a dentist and don&#x27;t know how many pounds per square inch are recommended to chase scum away from teeth and gum, but where I once started out clicking up the water pressure output to high, I now use it on the norm and am very happy with the results.  I cover all areas with one filling of water. The Dentist said my teeth and gum are looking good.    Additional Note:  Consider the physics behind using this thing - if you are in a big hurry and grab it with one hand in the middle section, the weight distribution could cause two things to occur: 1) you bang the spout around in your mouth in a very ineffective manner and believe this tool&#x27;s performance sucks, or 2) you learn to hold the spout away from sensitive areas of your mouth in an ineffective manner and feel disappointed in the tools inability to reach and penetrate those areas adequately. Try to stop viewing this thing as a quick, one-handed, gadget that works on it&#x27;s own.  It is only a battery operated, semi-waterproof, water-resistant, water squirting device. It won&#x27;t do much more of that by itself. If Waterpic told the world that this thing is tricky to use, they would sell very few of them - but in truth all sophisticated gadgets have their idiosyncrasies.  Each user must find a method to hold and operate the tool within its limitations and best capabilities. I use two hands, one near the bottom of the spout to steer it and one near the bottom to carry the weight (it isn&#x27;t really heavy, but the weight distribution(with water) deprives the accuracy of control I want). On low, I get plenty of pressure because I place the tip of the spout right up between teeth and between teeth and gums.       Tips:  Warm water (as when the shower is just about ready to be entered) may work better.   A little bit of Mouthwash mixed in with the water brings forth a refreshing result.   This is a shower gizmo - if you don&#x27;t intend to use this in the shower, you might prefer to get a sink model instead - they lack the weight, hold more water, and are easier to deal with.   As mentioned before, this is not a travel device - you&#x27;ll get water everywhere.   Don&#x27;t overcharge these types of electronics - Waterpik didn&#x27;t put a battery indicator, so now and then, it will quit - if it quits once - don&#x27;t use until it is fully recharged.  Once fully recharged, don&#x27;t charge it until it gets really slow or quits.     I gave it 4 starts because I don&#x27;t \\&quot;love\\&quot; my gadgets, nor did anything about this product \\&quot;blow me away\\&quot;.  But this product, for me, does what it was designed to do and what I expected it to do.  It is well built.  I wish it was designed a little lighter in weight, and had a better battery/charger system.</li>

The hygienist said that my gums were in excellent health and there was almost no plaque, so very little scraping!! So why only 3 stars? The unit has two brass posts that accept the recharging cord. These posts are susceptible to corrosion which if and when they corrode will affect the units ability to fully re-charge. I cleaned the posts with WD-40 and the unit is re-charging like new. If you get the unit (which I still recommend) spray the brass posts with WD-40 right away and you shouldn&#x27;t have any future recharging problems!</li>

    <li> I have had two rechargable Waterpiks. Both had the same problem. After about 5 or 10 months the unit gradually loses the ability to charge up. Most users assume that the battery became defective.     I really need this thing so I decided to look into it and found that the battery in each case was fine. What happens is that the connector on the charging cable gradually deteriorates. This might be due to getting wet repeatedly combined with corrosion and deposits. The inside of the female part of the connector gets get eaten away and actually gets larger in diameter. The electrical connection deteriorates and finally becomes unusable. As a result the battery no longer gets recharged.     I found that the \\&quot;AdaptaPlug\\&quot; connector system available at Radio Shack has the same pin diameter and pin spacing. By whittling some plastic away I made a better connector from the Radio Shack parts and now the Waterpiks work like new.     The part numbers of the Radio Shack connectors needed are:   Male: 273-1742   Female: 273-1743</li>
    <li> I love these.  The only reason I give it a 3 instead of 5 is that they wear out eventually and don&#x27;t take a charge.  I have had three of them and I believe they have lasted a little over a year, with twice daily use.</li>

    <li> My Dentist sold me on the product and the concept.  I&#x27;ve been using it everyday ever since.  I can honestly say the nylon string dental floss never inspired me. But (there is always one) the product is marred in terms of its expected lifespan and what I consider a flawed design which was a major annoyance to me.    Lifespan:  When it was new, I had to charge the battery once a  week. Over time, the frequency of the battery recharging between uses increased and after six months it stopped working.    Flawed Design:    The product has no battery charge indicator. As a result:   1) Its impossible to tell how much charge is left in the battery    2) When its being charged you don&#x27;t know if it has completed charging.    3) Or, if it is even charging - we have GFI outlets in our bathroom.  Frequently my wife&#x27;s hair dryer, after usage, trips the GFI circuit and as a result no power is supplied to all the circuits unless it is reset.  Therefore even though the Waterpik is plugged in, you don&#x27;t know if it getting charged until you go to use it or have to plug some other electrical product with an indicator to know power is being supplied.         The only other cordless oral hygiene product I can compare it to in terms of its lifespan and design is the Phillips sonic toothbrush,  My original toothbrush lasted 5+ years before dying and had indicator to inform you the level of charge left and/or amount of the battery charged during recharging.  I&#x27;m not sure how long I expected this product to last, but at the minimum at least two years, as this is the time of their limited warranty.  I would have given the product one star, but the ease with which theCustomer Service responded and agreed to send me a replacement (without having to send the broken product back) earns them additional two stars as I usually do not experience or expect this level of quality service in this day and age.    We will see how long the replacement product lasts.  The other interesting thing the Customer service person mentioned, which sounds counter intuitive to me, is that I need to keep the Waterpik plugged in all the time expect when it is in use.  I thought keeping a rechargeable battery plugged in all the time would reduce its lifespan.  The experts will have to chime in.</li>

    <li> Having had some form of waterpik from their beginning many years back, I have watched their models evolve and purchased many over the years.  Some good and some not so good.  It seemed the older more simple units lasted longer.  I purchased my WP-455W, in Orlando, FL @ Wallmart on a vacation trip as I left my counter top unit at home and needed one as a vacation back-up.  I find it mediocre in quality, somewhat messy until you figure out what angle to hold it while using it.  Your opinion of noisy is somewhat subjective as they all vary with use and age.  My point in reviewing this is a note to anyone using WaterPik products with serious allergies to MOLD.  As I noted in an earlier review of my experience with several of my last few counter top models......  BEWARE of MOLD buildup internally.....if you live in Gulf Coast or areas of high MOLD activity.  MOLD will eventually build up in the seams, and behind the tank in this model and you should regularly  remove your tank by the plastic clip on the bottom and pull down to remove the blue tank.  The plastic IS  fragile so be careful.  If you see any darkening on the white surfaces behind the attached tank it IS mold.  My suggestion is use an old toothbrush and spray some Hydrogen Peroxide while scrubbing with the tooth  brush...Hydrogen Peroxide kills mold.  It is less toxic to you than Clorox and less likely to ignite from a  spark from an electric motor than EverClear alcohol which is also good to kill mold.  I buy bulk containers of Hydrogen Peroxide @ Sam&#x27;s and use it in hand sprayers.  I would inspect every 90 days.  Too bad WP engineers don&#x27;t factor in the constant dampness in the units and mold possibilities and design  for this issue.  Update: 6/21/15  After thoroughly cleaning and removing the mold when I posted the original review.  I noticed the mold was in it&#x27;s earlier stage of a mildew appearance and will eventually reappear as black as it is allowed to age.  This is a reoccurring problem. I will post aphoto of the location.  Update: 5/18/16  I have grown weary of this mold issue and constant cleaning.  The unit sat for 4 months unused until I was about to take it on another trip out of town.  The mold has progressed internally.  I will not flush with clorox as it will compromise the pump and will definitely not be healthy.  I noticed that the pump was also getting weaker.  I will trash the WaterPic and use my Panasonic unit.     <li> OK, I didn&#x27;t read all the reviews, but here&#x27;s my take on this unit.  The unit works fine for what it was designed to do--no complaints there.  However, the big downside for me on this unit is the lack of a battery charge indicator.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why is the battery charge indicator SO IMPORTANT!  Because once you have discharged the batteries all the way down, which at some point everyone is going to do, you have just signed the death warrant of this unit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The nature of virtually all types of rechargeable batteries (in particular any lithium polymer battery, but also nicad&#x27;s, and nimh&#x27;s) is once you have taken the batteries down past 20% of there capacity you have immediately shortened their lifespan and limited there capacity to hold a full charge.  Every time you do this you degrade the battery that much more.  Once is all it takes and your batteries are on the way to the trash can.  And since you can&#x27;t replace the batteries in the unit, the whole thing is going into the trash.  It&#x27;s not going to happen right away, but the batteries will never be the same afterward.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It is critical, if you want this unit to last, to recharge it regularly and attempt to NEVER allow it to discharge all the way to where the unit stops working!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Waterpik could solve this issue easily in one of two ways.  1) put a charge indicator on the side of the unit, or better yet, 2) put rechargeable and REPLACEABLE AA-size nihm&#x27;s or nicad&#x27;s in the unit.  That way we all wouldn&#x27;t have to throw the baby out with the bath water when we inadvertently over discharge the batteries.  We could just order new batteries and replace them and not have to buy a new unit, which is what my wife and I have to do about every year or two.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Gee, I wonder why Waterpik didn&#x27;t do this in the first place?  He said sarcastically.</li>

    <li> Many complaints about the battery not accepting a charge after 3-4 months. Tilt the unit in the sink in a position that you can pour a few drops of white vinegar in the little hole where the two copper contact prongs are. Let soak for about 15 minutes then drain. With your breath, blow out the remaining vinegar and let the unit dry. Then recharge as usual. I learned this trick with my 20-year-old Mr. Coffee coffee pot. Our South Florida water is terrible and clogs my coffee pot. I run white vinegar through and then three more times with clear water and the unit is good as new. I did something similar with the waterpik. I believe the whole point of having a cordless waterpik is to use it in the shower, because using it at the sink is so messy. I don&#x27;t know if waterpik had this in mind when designing the cordless version. So, if others like me use the unit in the shower, the copper points are going to corrode like terminals on a car battery. Vinegar eats away the corrosion. On another note, my dentist suggested running hydrogen-peroxide through the waterpik and after finishing, let the unit run a cycle of clear water through it. I do all this while in the shower. I guess it may eventually clog but after 8 months, it still works fine. I&#x27;ll just run white vinegar through it if it starts to clog. Other than that, I love the product. My dentist is thrilled with my checkups.</li>

Plus the on button moves so easily I keep accidentally touching it when removing the tip from my mouth or getting ready to use it and spraying mouthwash in my face, on my shirt or across the room! :-) I finally wrapped a rubber band between the tip holder and the body so it wouldn&#x27;t move without some effort and another over the on/off button and around the body pulling it down toward the off position so it shuts off when I stop pushing on it.     <li> I&#x27;ve used both a Water Pik brand \\&quot;oral irrigator\\&quot; and then, after that died, an Interplak unit.  Both of these were the standard counter-top type with a reservoir on top and the nozzle/handle connected by a small hose.  They both worked great, but died after a few years of steady use.  Not really that bad of life for such a gadget, I think.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I wanted to replace the last one to die, so I visited a couple of well-known department stores in my town.  The first one didn&#x27;t have what I was looking for, so I tried the other one, and it didn&#x27;t have what I really wanted either.  So, thinking it might work OK anyhow, I settled for one of these Water Pik Watterflosser cordless plus hand-held rechargeable units.  It seems kind of odd that nobody around here carries any of the standard countertop units right now. (Of course, Amazon does, and I now have one of the standard countertop units on order).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This cordless unit has turned out to be extremely disappointing. I charged it for 24 hours prior to the first use, just as instructed. I then filled it and gave it a try.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The first thing I noticed was that it really was very loud.  My wife commented on it immediately.  So you&#x27;d never be able to get away with using it while someone else in the house was trying to sleep.  It did a good job of terrifying the cats, too.  ;-)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The next thing I noticed was that, try as I might, there was no way to get all of the desired angles without causing the unit to suck air because the reservoir, naturally, must move with the handle.  Since the unit can only suck up water when it&#x27;s being held more or less vertically, that seriously restricts the possible aim angles of the nozzle.  Unless you can stand on your head in the sink, it&#x27;s quite a drawback.  Just try getting the backs of your lower teeth with it.  Not very easy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of course, I should have realized this obvious drawback before buying such a design, but for whatever reason, I figured that theymight have worked things out to let it pull water out of the reservoir with it in a number of different orientations.  But I freely admit that I can&#x27;t think of how such a system could be worked out without some complex system of automatically-operated valves or the like.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The third drawback was the extremely short time that it runs before needing to be refilled.  I was using it on high (because the low setting was so \\&quot;limp\\&quot; as to be useless) and the reservoir proved to yield only enough run-time to get me about 1/4 of the way finished with the job.  It might run longer on the low setting, but, again, that&#x27;d be completely useless.  I can swish water around my mouth with more force than the low setting generates.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I guess I&#x27;ve just been spoiled by the way the two \\&quot;countertop\\&quot; style units I&#x27;ve had before operated.  Both had FAR more power (needing to be set well below their highest settings for my use), ran for about five to ten times as long on a filling, and allowed me to easily and successfully direct the stream at every point where gums meet tooth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Again, I should have realized that an \\&quot;all in one\\&quot; style unit simply could not work the way I wanted it to, but I guess I simply didn&#x27;t think it through and imagined that it&#x27;d work well since it was being sold as a viable product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I took it back to the retailer where I got it, and they gave me my money back, no questions asked, even though I told them that there was no \\&quot;defect\\&quot; in the unit, only that it simply did not do what I needed it to do.  So Kudos to that national chain for their returns policy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The bad thing is that Water Pik may never know why it was returned.  They&#x27;ll probably figure some bonehead didn&#x27;t know how to charge it or fill it or something like that.  But seriously:  They really ought to try using this thing before even going into production.  If all I wanted to do was spray the fronts of my teeth with it very briefly, I can see how it&#x27;d accomplishthat.  But if someone wants to get the backs of their bottom teeth, I&#x27;d love to see how that works.  I guess you could tip your head to the side one way for one half, then to the other for the other half, but it&#x27;s really a pain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Nope.  My assessment is that it&#x27;s too loud, too weak, runs out of water way too fast, and is difficult to manipulate to get all of the \\&quot;targets\\&quot; without it sucking air.  As attractive as the whole cordless concept may be, the fact is that a standard base unit with a generous reservoir and a small, easy-to-aim handpiece connected by a small hose turns out to be the best design in my experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For those who like this unit.  That&#x27;s great.  I hope it works well for you for many years.  But if you&#x27;re considering it, and are either used to the table-top version or have never tried any of these units, my advice is to stay (or start) with the countertop style that&#x27;s been tried and proven for years.</li>

    <li> Several years after I bought it, the product is still usable. I&#x27;ve had the often reported charger contacts corrosion problem just over a year after I bought the item. Repaired it myself. Two years later, the stock battery became weak, wouldn&#x27;t hold a charge for a while. The charging circuit in this device is way too primitive. There is a schottky diode between the battery and the charging contacts, which drops voltage from the charger (3V) down to 2.45V, that&#x27;s all. This prevents overcharging the battery, however the battery is never charged to full capacity. I&#x27;ve replaced the ni-mh battery in mine with a cheap new ni-mh battery from China, removed the diode from the circuit, and replaced the charger with a cheap universal ni-mh charger from China. Used an automotive miniature waterproof connector (AMP SuperSeal 2-position) as a connector, to prevent corrosion of the charger terminals. By the way, every time I had to service the electrics in this device, I had to disassemble everything, since the electrics are the deepest hidden part in the case.&lt;br /&gt;If I had to choose again, I would probably buy a corded version...</li>

I literally had to plug it in over night and bet on the 50/50 chance of it actually charging or not depending on pure luck!    Secondly, for a device that is meant to be used in an environment full of water for an activity that involves a lot of water flowing and splashing around, it is not exactly water proof.  It gets wet inside and causes all kinds of problems including biological things that grow inside (eeew)    The electric motor just rusted and got stuck after a few months so I had to take it apart and service it like a car - which is not something an average user would be able to do.    The nozzle sometime pops out of the main unit especially at the high pressure setting.    It is pretty noisy to begin with and gets worse as it ages. But if you close the door of your bathroom you might be able to get away with it.    The water tank is very small and I usually took about 3 refills on a normal cleanup.    Finally after about one year, the gears that make contact between the motor and the pump simply kept skipping and it got to a point beyond repair even for somebody like me who really kept trying hard to make it work.I&#x27;m planning not to replace this with the same unit and try one of those simpler attach to the tap type ones instead next time.  One major disadvantage is I won&#x27;t have the option of using mouthwash (e.g. Listerine) instead of water alone in the spray with it.    But don&#x27;t get me wrong, despite wearing braces, my hygienist complimented about how clean I maintained my teeth and good part of the credit should go to this device.  If only it was a bit more reliable and user friendly.  So do try it but don&#x27;t expect it to be perfect.</li>
    <li> My last Waterpik was the standard countertop version with a hose.  I thought this would take up less counterspace, and it does, but it is not much fun to use.  The cordless version is just too bulky to be comfortable in use.  Another problem is the tips rotate too easily - it is difficult to keep the stream of water aimed where you want it unless you use both hands, one to hold the unit and the other holding the tip. It also has a fairly weak pump - even fully charged it often stops while using.  Finally, the tank does not hold enough water.  Even on low power setting it is empty before you hit all your teeth. As it empties you need to juggle the unit to keep the pump intake underwater.    All in all, even though the countertop version takes up more space, it is the way to go.</li>
    <li> what a mess! water everywhere, can&#x27;t open your lips to even see what you&#x27;re doing due to all the splashing.  am returning this and buying a sonicare.  hope it works better.</li>
    <li> I have used A Waterpick  device for years, but this model is very easy to use and easy to keep clean!  It takes up less room on the counter, too</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve owned my Ultra Cordless for about 6 months now, and feel that enough time has gone by to write a review.  Some of categories I have been keeping an eye on are:  1) Battery Charge Intervals 2) Reservoir Size 3) Jet Power  4) Ergonomics  5) Construction Quality  6) Corrosion at recharge terminal  7) Power Switch reliability  8) Noise  9) Transportability  10) Effectiveness of oral irrigation.    1) The battery charge interval is outstanding. I use the unit twice a day on average, and I can go more than three weeks between charges.  Each use of the unit drains the fully filled reservoir.  I let the battery completely discharge through use, then fully recharge on the charger overnight for more than 12 hours.    2) Rerservoir size, on full power setting, is more than adequate to fully irrigate for me.  I find no issues with the size.    3) Jet Power, has two settings.  I use the full power setting, and it seems to have enough power with a fairly strong jet.  When I first started using the Ultra, I had to start on the low setting due to gum sensitivity.    4) The unit has a tapered area that makes it easy to hold.  Also, the tank design weighs the unit such that it is comfortable to the hand.      5) Construction quality seems good, with quality plastics.  It is made in China.    6) Corrosion at recharge terminal.  The terminal socket has pins that are gold plated.  Even though it gets wet during use, there is no corrosion in the terminal socket, as would be expected from gold plated pins.    7) Power on/off switch reliability.  This is a slider switch, and it gets wet during use.  It does not appear to be water proof by way of external examination.  However, it is working fine after 6 months, and doesn&#x27;t appear to be suffering any degradation.  It is something I will continue to keep an eye on.    8) Noise.  The pump makes noise, and any insulation would add weight.  The pump is fairly powerful for a battery powered unit, so some noise is a good engineering compromise. I don&#x27;t find the noise excessive.     9) Transportability.  I take my Ultra on trips and use it at home.  I take off the reservoir tank and pull off the jet tip for transport.  The three small items can pack neatly in your luggage.  I&#x27;m pleased that the unit is easily transportable.    10) Effectiveness.  My gums are much healthier and exhibit a pink color.  If you have red gums, then that means you have some infection setting in.  Irrigating with the Ultra and using a small amount of mouthwash (like Listerene) kills plaque forming bacteria.  The jet removes food particles and some of the mouthwash \\&quot;chemistry\\&quot; gets under the gumline to help preserve gum health.     The niggles are that the jet tip rotates in its socket.  You have to use two hands, one to hold the jet tip at the base, and the other to hold the unit.  The jet tip should be keyed to the knurled collar.  The power switch is a concern for longevity, but this worry could be unwarranted.  It doesn&#x27;t seem obvious how to replace the battery if and when it fails.  Without the niggles, this could be a five star product, but I give four stars for a pretty solid showing.</li>

But seriously, this thing just sucks. The fact that it did actually work, and kinda decently, for a couple months, is the only reason it didn&#x27;t get a 1-star.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;WARNING! GEEK LEVEL ANALYSIS AHEAD:&lt;br /&gt;I work on electronics for a living, so i know a thing or two. When this thing&#x27;s battery died, i took it apart to figure out what went wrong. It&#x27;s poorly designed. The charger doesn&#x27;t create DC power, which is what ALL batteries charge on. No, it converts 110vac to 3vac, and then uses a diode to sorta kinda turn that into pulsed DC, and THAT is what charges it. I think this explains the long charge times and the lame battery life. So, to &#x27;fix&#x27; it, i took the battery out, and modified it so that the charging cord hooked straight to the motor, and set up a few Dcell batteries to act as its power source. That&#x27;s working ok so far.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*update - died a few weeks after my D cell mod.extra amps and volts probably fried the motor.</li>

    <li> Used one of the original plug-in-the-wall Pik units back in the &#x27;60s as a kid. Considered it a chore. 50 years later, with gingival issues, I didn&#x27;t realize then how important it was.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The PLUS is a great product. Battery good for about 2 weeks of use (once with regular tip, once with pocket-pic, daily,) and a large enough water reservoir. You can safely ignore the poor guy who complained about the tip \\&quot;spinning around\\&quot; because he was too ignorant or stupid to actually insert the tip into the unit properly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I recommend it to everyone. Gingivitis (which affects almost everyone, eventually) can lead to increasing pocket depths, which contributes to bone loss, which, if bad enough, will lead to tooth loss. Those scary pamphlets in your dentist&#x27;s office have a valid point.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Not a good road to go down, unless you admire the toothless hillbilly look. There have been many published dental studies (I read about 40 of them on-line in the Journal of Periodontology) that confirm the efficacy of disruption of bacteria whether physically or chemically (by, say, chlorhexidine,) and the PLUS (and Pocket-Pik tip) are good tools in that ongoing war. Cheap at twice the price, but don&#x27;t use it to remove ear wax (one study details how you&#x27;ll rupture your eardrum.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After about a month of use, it seems to be consistently good for about 2 dozen or so uses between charges.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Speaking of charging, someone commented about corrosion on the charging contact pins. It&#x27;s true -- I noticed minor corrosion almost immediately. It would have been better if Water-Pik had provided some sort of plug/barrier to keep water out of the plug-in cavity, or, better yet if they had used an induction-charge system with no contact points or pins as do many electric toothbrushes and other devices (either would make the product slightly more expensive, the later more so, but it would be well worth the extra dollar or three.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But, unfortunately, they didn&#x27;t. Nonetheless, the corrosion problem is easily solved without buying any Radio Shack parts. Carefully scrape any minor corrosion off of the pins with the tip of a knife and use an inch of tape (anything that&#x27;s about 1/2\\&quot; wide) over the plug-in cavity to keep water out of the plug-in cavity while in use between charges.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hopefully, they read this stuff and will either add some sort of (attached to the unit) plug or go to an induction-type re-charge method on the next version of the PLUS, if they haven&#x27;t already concluded that one or the other is a good idea.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In any case, I still HIGHLY recommend the PLUS. It gets all sorts of stuff out of your mouth that brushing and flossing can&#x27;t and don&#x27;t.</li>

Have to say that they didn&#x27;t bother with shipping them to US for replacements. After using my new flosser for a little bit over a year it died and stopped charging. This time the company customer service wasn&#x27;t that nice and didn&#x27;t replace the unit as it has been over two years from the original purchase date. So if you plan to buy it be cautious because they replace the product under the warranty only once! I am disappointed in this product as I bought 3 of them and ALL broke after about a year of daily use. This time I&#x27;m going to find something more reliable.</li>
    <li> Counter tops? No, just charge this thing up and put it in your shower, don&#x27;t worry about making a mess, life is so easy now, wish someone would&#x27;ve told me this 10 years ago.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Regarding the charging not working after a few months (as many people have complained about), the other reviewer here correctly explained the issue (the contact points stop contacting the cord to receive the charge). The other reviewer suggested getting a different charging cord that had a tighter fit, but the solution I found was just use a bobby pin to clean off the funk that builds on the charging tips on the device. Its a poor design, being \\&quot;level\\&quot; the water can accumulate there &amp; build deposits on the tips, preventing the charge from transferring. Just clean off the charging tips so the juice can flow across, easy fix.</li>

    <li> My dentist says that since I am using this pic every day that my gum condition has improved.  This pic can be used away from the electric socket as most pics have short cords.  I take it into the shower with me to avoid a mess.</li>
    <li> I purchased a used or display model at discount and paid dearly for the good deal in the long run.  Upon receipt the pump was feeble.  I took it apart and found that one of the pump reed valves was deformed but easily fixed.  After that the unit only ran two to three tanks of water before it was too pooped to pump.  I rigged a voltmeter to the battery terminals and found out that voltage dropped to under 1.25v when the pump was running:  Clearly, the batteries were dying and would not take a charge.      I took it apart and noted that the batteries were two solder-tab style AA size Nickel-metal hydride - NiMh- 1.2v cells wired in series.  They were in shrink wrap that said 2.4v, 1500 Milli&#x3D;ampHour - MaH.  I installed a pair of 1.2V, 2500 mah cells from the auction site.  Wow - it&#x27;s a different machine:  The motor runs faster and the pump puts out a far better stream of water.  So far it has emptied over ten tanks of water and is still going strong on the first charge.    I&#x27;ll note here that there is a &#x27;dry&#x27; side of the unit that is sealed against moisture.  The seal had failed and the battery was fairly corroded.  The motor casing and on/off switch had superficial corrosion.  I applied a corrosion inhibitor called Corrosion-X before reassembly.    Now that it&#x27;s running right I&#x27;m considering the installation of a charge LED so I know the batteries are charging.  And maybe install air vents and water drains, since I know it will get inside.  Or add a door and appropriate connectors to the battery compartment so I can use disposable batteries and eliminate the charger.    Batteries are living things, and unless new, corrosion free and kept on a charger they become an unknown quantity.  Also, not knowing how long the machine sat on the shelf with the internals corroding before I bought it, it seems only fair to allow for a dead battery and score it as it runs after repair.  If I ran into these problems with a new unit at list prices I would not be so generous.  Ditto ifI weren&#x27;t so handy and consider these things challenges.  Bu then, I would have returned it.    In the interim I got the Panasonic oral irrigator and love it:  they fixed the one weakness of the Waterflosser:  - dead or dying batteries -by making them replaceable; which also eliminates the problem of lost chargers and corroded connectors.  The Panasonic also collapses the power head into the tank, so it travels small.  http://www.amazon.com/Panasonic-EW-DJ10-A-Oral-Irrigator/dp/B0027LSEPS</li>

The positive reviews that answer all the negatives are pretty much dead-on, folks, and you can buy this in confidence. The best advice is to keep the power jack wires clean even though there&#x27;s no way to keep them dry, and I am blowing out the water in the jack after every use and will use the vinnegar technique if deposits form. Unfortunately, water continues to drain down into the jacks even after you thoroughly dry the unit... probably not a serious issue if you&#x27;re keeping them clean, though.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s powerful enough on the low setting to pik through the spaces between teeth, though quite a bit less than the counter top model. The high power setting is sufficient for cleaning with any of the standard piks; I do not need any more power. It&#x27;s a comfortable pressure but won&#x27;t give you that stinging sensation of the counter top.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The reservoir is on an angle and it is easy to under-fill it, though once you realize this it is easy to fill it all the way. The first time I used this I ran out of water, but the second time the extra fill gave me about 10 more seconds. Also, I save a little room to add a bit of listerene just before closing the latch. If I run out of water, I&#x27;m right there at the faucet anyway so it just takes a coupld of seconds to add a little more. You can&#x27;t fill and re-insert the tank because there is a litte hole on the bottom where the pik draws the water, but I&#x27;d prefer to fill while it is attached anyway.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It is not loud. It sounds just like the countertop model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There is a little learning curve to holding the unit, but by the second use I was able to do the outside and inside of mygums. The countertop model is much more easily manipulated, of course. You have to keep your head down with this one, so it is messy but everything goes in the sink and it doesn&#x27;t spray out unless you take it out of your mouth. The head does not move around freely but it is easily moved, and this can take some getting used to but is not a problem after a couple of uses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The unit gets completely wet during use. Rinsing it off, opening the latch to shake out water left in the tank, drying it on my bathtowel and blowing a little air in the jack takes a couple of seconds. As I noted, a little water continues to drop down from somewhere and some of this can get into the jack, but it is all well sealed and does not seem to make a difference.     <li> I bought the WP450 cordless model in June 2012, after repeated 6-month dentist appointments with ever deepening \\&quot;pockets\\&quot; and me saying: OK, I&#x27;ll try harder, brush better, floss better/more often, reach those corners better.     <li> I recently purchased my second unit [third if I count the one I gave my spouse]. The first lasted 2 years. I was pretty annoyed about that until I read on this site the positive customer review that included a detailed and well-conceived explanation about the care and charging of the battery. I had started shopping for a new device, determined to never purchase another WaterPik flosser. After reading that review, I checked the terminals on my unit and sure enough they were corroded. I always kept the first unit connected to the charger when not in use. I did wipe the unit each time, but I did not spend much time drying the terminals, if at all. Now I place a piece of clear tape over the terminals until the unit needs to be charged; I only charge the unit when the battery is spent. No wet, corroding terminals and the unit seems as powerful as the first time I used it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I really like this device, except for the cost.     <li> This waterflosser is fantastic! The flow of water is quite strong, the portability of it allows me to use it in a small bathroom where I have no room for our older Waterpik flosser. And if the reservoir were any bigger, I think the unit would be too cumbersome to handle. Finally,be sure to charge it for a full 24 hours before using, then keep it plugged in except for when you&#x27;re using it, this way it keeps a charge beautifully. I use my flosser one or two times a day, and I have no trouble with it being fully charged every time. I love this thing!&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: As others have noticed, this unit starts having problems with staying charged. It is not that the battery does not hold the charge, but that the cord does not fit snugly into the unit so it does not charge the battery. I have found that jamming a very narrow piece of plastic (or other non-metal item) the thickness of a credit card into a tiny gap above the cord where it is plugged into the unit will create the contact necessary for the battery to receive the charge. Once I figured this out, my unit went back to full power. No need to purchase anything additional! (And don&#x27;t forget to disconnect the unit from the cord when in use.)</li>
